## **MKT-25-churn-campaign – Win-Back & Churn Prevention Playbook**

* ID: MKT-25-churn-campaign  
* Pain Point Statement: Lapsed or at-risk customers receive no targeted win-back or save campaigns.  
* Impact Level (1–10): 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Lost recurring revenue and referrals from preventable churn.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high for subscription or repeat-purchase businesses.  
* SEO Title: “AI churn prevention and win-back email campaign generator”  
* SEO Optimized Copy: “Create targeted churn prevention and win-back campaigns with tailored messaging based on customer behavior and reasons for leaving.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You have subscriptions, memberships, or repeat purchase patterns.  
  * Churn is rising or higher than benchmarks.  
  * You have basic lifecycle or cancellation data.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Customers are leaving due to serious product failures you haven’t addressed.  
  * Contractual or legal reasons prevent re-contact.  
  * You lack any way to segment active vs lapsed.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Definitions of at-risk and lapsed customers.  
  * Common cancellation reasons and objections.  
  * Available incentives (discounts, bonuses, check-ins).  
  * Channels to reach past customers (email, SMS, in-app).  
* Deliverables:  
  * A set of 5–10 win-back and save campaign emails/messages with segmentation notes and timing recommendations.  
* SEO One-liner: “Reduce churn and revive lost customers with AI-crafted win-back and save campaigns.”

# SAL \- Sales

## **SAL-01-lead-qualifier — Lead Qualification Matrix & Script**

* Pain Point: Reps chase anyone who shows interest, filling the pipeline with unqualified opportunities.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Unqualified pipeline bloats forecasts and wastes rep time, lowering win rates and driving burnout.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high upside in focus and conversion.  
* SEO Title: “AI lead qualification framework and script generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Define clear qualification criteria and scripts so reps quickly separate high-value opportunities from noise.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * Lead volume is decent but win rates are poor.  
  * Marketing and sales argue over lead quality.  
  * Reps complain about “wasting time” on bad fits.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Lead volume is extremely low, so you must talk to almost everyone.  
  * ICP is still unknown; you’re in pure discovery mode.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Your ICP and core segments.  
  * History of closed-won vs closed-lost deals.  
  * Current discovery questions and forms.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Qualification matrix (fit and intent criteria).  
  * Call/email scripts calibrated to quickly surface disqualifiers.  
* SEO One-liner: “Give reps an AI-built qualification framework to focus on deals that can actually close.”

---

## **SAL-02-call-openers — Cold Call & Pattern Interrupt Openers**

* Pain Point: Cold calls start with generic intros that get shut down instantly.  
* Impact Level: 7  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Low connect and conversation rates limit pipeline from phone-based outreach.  
* Effort vs. Value: Low; fast improvement in live conversations.  
* SEO Title: “AI cold call opener and pattern interrupt generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Create tested-style cold call openers and pattern interrupts that reduce brush-offs and start real conversations.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * SDRs or founders use the phone and see low call talk time.  
  * Reps struggle with confidence in their first 10 seconds.  
  * You’re entering new segments and need tailored openers.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Outbound calling is not part of your motion.  
  * Compliance or scripts are heavily regulated.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Target persona roles and typical day-in-the-life.  
  * Your core value props and offer.  
  * Any legal script requirements.  
* Deliverables:  
  * A set of openers, pattern interrupts, and pivots for each persona.  
* SEO One-liner: “Open more cold calls with AI-crafted pattern interrupts that buyers actually respond to.”

---

## **SAL-03-outbound-templates — Outbound Email Template Pack**

* Pain Point: Outbound emails are long, generic, and ignored.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Low open and reply rates starve the top of the pipeline.  
* Effort vs. Value: Low–medium; high leverage on new pipeline.  
* SEO Title: “AI outbound sales email template generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Generate concise, persona-specific outbound email templates with clear hooks and CTAs that fit modern inbox behavior.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re spinning up an SDR function or founder-led outbound.  
  * Campaign metrics (opens, replies) are weak.  
  * Reps each write their own untested emails.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You rely solely on inbound or partner-driven deals.  
  * Cold emailing is restricted in your jurisdictions/markets.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Target personas and their pains.  
  * Offers and proof points.  
  * Channel limits and opt-out policies.  
* Deliverables:  
  * 4–8 short email templates per persona with subject lines, bodies, and PS ideas.  
* SEO One-liner: “Equip your outbound motion with short, sharp AI-written email templates that earn replies.”

## **SAL-04-discovery-scripts — Discovery Call Script Designer**

* Pain Point: Reps wing discovery, miss key context, and fail to quantify pain or impact.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Poor discovery leads to long cycles, weak proposals, and “no decision” losses.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high leverage on deal quality.

* SEO Copy: “Design high-impact discovery call scripts with smart questions that uncover budget, authority, pain, and timing without sounding robotic.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * “Good first calls” don’t turn into real opportunities.  
  * New reps struggle to know what to ask.  
  * You’re standardizing on a sales methodology.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Calls are quick transactional orders with minimal qualification.  
  * Stringent regulations dictate the question set.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * ICP and stakeholder types.  
  * Current discovery formats or methodologies (MEDDIC, SPICED, etc.).  
  * Common pains, use cases, and objections.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Discovery script with opener, context-setting, question flow, and recap/next-step language.  
* SEO One-liner: “Run tighter discovery calls that surface real pain and clear next steps using AI-built scripts.”

  * You’re rolling out new features or repositioning.

## **SAL-06-followup-cadences — Follow-Up Cadence & Template Engine**

* Pain Point: Follow-up is inconsistent; reps give up after one or two touches.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Deals die of neglect even when interest exists.  
* Effort vs. Value: Low–medium; huge impact on progression and show rates.

* Deploy When:  
  * You have lots of “went quiet” opportunities.  
  * There’s no agreed standard on touches or time span.  
  * Calendar no-shows are common.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Compliance strictly limits outreach frequency.  
  * You already run coordinated, well-performing cadences.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Lead sources and typical sales cycles.  
  * Allowed channels (email, phone, LinkedIn, SMS).  
  * Current follow-up patterns and metrics.  
* Deliverables:  
  * 7–14 touch cadence designs per segment with message templates and task guidance.  
* SEO One-liner: “Standardize persistent, respectful follow-ups that revive silent deals and boost response rates.”

  * Deals are instant purchases in-app with no proposals.

## **SAL-15-pricing-guardrails — Discount & Pricing Guardrail Sheet**

* Pain Point: Reps discount inconsistently and create pricing surprises internally.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Margin erosion and fraught approvals slow deals.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong impact on profitability and trust.  
* SEO Title: “AI sales pricing and discount guardrail template”  
* SEO Copy: “Define clear pricing and discount guardrails so reps know when and how far they can go without killing margins.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * Discounts vary wildly by rep or deal.  
  * Finance frequently escalates or rejects deals.  
  * You’re moving upmarket or into larger deals.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Pricing is fully fixed and non-negotiable.  
  * You’re still very early and experimenting with price.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List prices, packages, and costs/margins.  
  * Historic discounting patterns and rationale.  
  * Approval flows and decision-makers.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Guardrail sheet outlining discount bands, conditions, and required approvals.  
  * Talk tracks for value-based pricing conversations.  
* SEO One-liner: “Stop random discounting with AI-defined pricing guardrails that protect your margins.”

# OPS \- Operations

## **OPS-01-sop-gen — SOP & Process Documentation Generator**

* Pain Point: Critical processes live in people’s heads instead of clear, repeatable SOPs, so quality depends on who is on shift.  
* Impact Level: 10  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Lack of documentation drives errors, rework, and stalled scaling; training and delegation become painfully slow.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium effort; extremely high leverage on quality, training, and resilience.  
* SEO Title: “AI SOP generator for small business operations”  
* SEO Copy: “Turn tribal knowledge into clear SOPs and checklists so your team can run key processes the same way every time.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You rely on a few “indispensable” people who hold all the know-how.  
  * New hires learn by shadowing and asking the same questions repeatedly.  
  * Quality varies wildly between shifts or locations.  
* Abstain When:  
  * The process truly changes week-to-week and is still being invented.  
  * You are about to throw out the workflow and replace it entirely.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * High-level description of the process and desired outcome.  
  * Notes, screenshots, or recordings of someone doing the work.  
  * Roles involved and tools/systems used.  
  * Any compliance or quality requirements.  
* Deliverables:  
  * One structured SOP per process with purpose, scope, step-by-step instructions, roles, inputs/outputs, and acceptance criteria.  
  * Optional checklist-format version for daily execution.  
* SEO One-liner: “Capture and standardize your core workflows with AI-generated SOPs your whole team can follow.”

---

## **OPS-02-process-map — Process Mapping & Bottleneck Finder**

* Pain Point: Leaders sense “operational chaos” but can’t see the end-to-end flow, so they guess where to fix things.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Hidden bottlenecks and broken handoffs cause delays, customer issues, and wasted effort.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; high clarity payoff for scaling and automation.  
* SEO Title: “AI business process map and bottleneck analysis generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Visualize your end-to-end workflows and surface bottlenecks so you know exactly where to improve operations first.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * Work gets “stuck” but no one agrees where.  
  * You plan to introduce new tools or automation.  
  * You want to reduce turnaround times or error rates on a core process.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You have almost no repeatable workflows yet (pure experimentation).  
  * An external consultant is already running a deep BPM exercise.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Description of the process start and end points.  
  * Roles and systems at each stage.  
  * Approximate timings and pain points from the team.  
  * Any existing diagrams or notes.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Narrative process map broken into stages with owners, inputs, and outputs.  
  * Short bottleneck report with 3–7 concrete improvement ideas.  
* SEO One-liner: “Expose and fix operational bottlenecks with AI-built process maps and improvement ideas.”

---

## **OPS-03-workflow-automation — Workflow Automation Blueprint**

* Pain Point: Teams burn hours on “swivel chair” tasks—copy/paste, status updates, manual reminders—instead of real work.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Manual workflows slow everything down, increase error risk, and make scaling headcount-intensive.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; very high ROI when focused on high-volume workflows.  
* SEO Title: “AI workflow automation use case and blueprint generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Identify high-impact automation opportunities and define the triggers, actions, and data flow to build them in your tools.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * Staff repeat identical steps dozens of times per day.  
  * Tickets, requests, or approvals pile up in inboxes.  
  * You’re rolling out an automation platform and need a roadmap.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Processes are unstable and changing weekly.  
  * Your stack has no API/integration options and can’t be automated at all.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of repetitive tasks by team and tool.  
  * Systems in use (CRM, support desk, project tools, etc.).  
  * Daily/weekly volumes and rough handling times.  
  * Constraints around approvals, security, and compliance.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Ranked automation backlog with impact/effort notes.  
  * Blueprint per shortlisted flow: trigger, conditions, actions, exceptions.  
* SEO One-liner: “Find and design AI-powered automations that eliminate busywork and speed up operations.”

## **OPS-04-onboarding-ops — Employee Onboarding Operations Checklist**

* Pain Point: New hires show up and spend days chasing logins, equipment, and information.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Slow ramp time, low early engagement, and avoidable mistakes.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong impact on productivity and retention.  
* SEO Title: “AI employee onboarding checklist and ops playbook generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Standardize employee onboarding with a step-by-step checklist and task list for HR, IT, and managers.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You regularly add staff or contractors.  
  * Onboarding tasks are managed via ad-hoc emails or memory.  
  * New hires frequently report “no one told me / I don’t have access.”  
* Abstain When:  
  * You already have a documented, enforced onboarding program that works.  
  * You have no hiring planned in the foreseeable future.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Role and department types you hire for.  
  * Systems, equipment, and access each role needs.  
  * Compliance or policy requirements (training, forms, etc.).  
  * Existing onboarding steps or timelines.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Role-specific onboarding checklists broken down by owner and timeframe (pre-day-1, week 1, days 30/60/90).  
  * A short onboarding process guide describing how it all fits together.  
* SEO One-liner: “Give every new hire a smooth start with AI-generated onboarding checklists and playbooks.”

## **OPS-05-offboarding-ops — Offboarding & Access Revocation Checklist**

* Pain Point: Departing staff leave with active accounts, open access, and undocumented knowledge.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Elevated security risk, IP leakage, and operational gaps during transitions.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; high risk-reduction and continuity value.  
* SEO Title: “AI employee offboarding checklist and access removal workflow”  
* SEO Copy: “Create a structured offboarding checklist that revokes access, captures knowledge, and protects your business.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You use many different SaaS tools and shared drives.  
  * Recent departures exposed missed access removal or data transfers.  
  * You’re growing and want to professionalize HR/IT processes.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You’re a solo operator or tiny team with minimal tools.  
  * You already follow strict, audited offboarding policies.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of systems and physical assets staff use.  
  * Typical roles and access patterns.  
  * Legal or compliance rules for data/devices.  
  * Any existing offboarding steps.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Role-specific offboarding checklists for HR, IT, and managers.  
  * Knowledge transfer prompts and asset recovery steps.  
* SEO One-liner: “Reduce risk and protect knowledge with AI-built offboarding checklists and access workflows.”

  * You’re selecting new software, logistics, or service providers.

  * You’ve had issues with unreliable or expensive suppliers.  
* Abstain When:

## **OPS-07-inventory-par-levels — Inventory PAR Level & Reorder Guide**

* Pain Point: Teams oscillate between stockouts and overstock because reorder points are guesswork.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Stockouts lose revenue and trust; overstock locks up cash and leads to spoilage or obsolescence.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high for any product or supply-heavy business.  
* SEO Title: “AI inventory par level and reorder point suggestion generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Use demand and lead time data to generate par levels and reorder guidelines that reduce stockouts and excess inventory.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You manage physical inventory, materials, or consumables.  
  * You frequently run out of key items or carry excessive surplus.  
  * You are not ready for full-blown demand planning software.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You only sell services or digital products.  
  * You already have mature demand planning and inventory systems in place.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * SKU list with historic sales/consumption.  
  * Supplier lead times and minimum order quantities.  
  * Storage limits and approximate carrying costs.  
  * Seasonality or promotional patterns.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Suggested par levels and reorder triggers per SKU or group.  
  * Plain-language notes on assumptions and how to tune over time.  
* SEO One-liner: “Set smarter inventory levels with AI-suggested par and reorder points tailored to your demand patterns.”

* Deliverables:

* SEO One-liner: “Balance workloads and staffing with AI-generated capacity planning and scheduling briefs.”

* Pain Point: When systems or processes break, the response is improvised and inconsistent.

* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; very high value where uptime and quality matter.

* SEO Copy: “Standardize how your team responds to outages, quality issues, or security events with clear, role-based playbooks.”  
* Deploy When:

  * Customers or partners expect formal incident response.  
* Abstain When:

  * Impact of incidents is trivial and quickly reversible.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of likely incident types (IT, facilities, safety, quality, etc.).

  * Roles, on-call rotations, and contact methods.  
  * Regulatory or contractual response requirements.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Playbooks per incident type (detect, triage, contain, communicate, resolve, review).  
  * Escalation matrix and stakeholder communication templates.  
* SEO One-liner: “Respond faster and more consistently to operational incidents with AI-created playbooks.”

* Impact Level: 9

* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; extremely high value for resilience.

  * You rely on a small number of key systems, sites, or vendors.  
  * Recent events (storms, outages, supply issues) exposed fragility.  
  * Customers or partners ask about your continuity posture.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You already maintain a formal BCP/DR program.  
  * Your operations are low-risk and easily paused.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of critical processes and dependencies.  
  * Acceptable downtime and data loss for each.  
  * Existing backups or alternate arrangements.  
* Deliverables:

  * Priority matrix for what to restore in what order.  
* SEO One-liner: “Make your business harder to knock offline with an AI-generated continuity playbook.”

# FIN \- Finance

## **FIN-01-cashflow-forecast — 13-Week Cash Flow Forecast Builder**

* Pain Point: Owners and operators fly blind on cash timing, only reacting when the bank balance looks scary. Cash flow uncertainty is now a top concern for small businesses.  
* Impact Level: 10  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without a forecast, you risk payroll crunches, missed payments, and missed growth opportunities; with one, you can see dips weeks ahead.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; extremely high leverage as an “early warning system.”  
* SEO Title: “AI 13-week cash flow forecast template for small businesses”  
* SEO Copy: “Generate a simple, spreadsheet-ready 13-week cash flow forecast so you can see cash crunches before they hit and plan growth with confidence.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’ve had cash squeezes or are worried about upcoming obligations.  
  * You’re planning hiring, a new location, or major spend.  
  * Lenders or investors want visibility into cash runway.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You have no transaction records at all; bookkeeping is non-existent (fix books first).  
  * Very early pre-revenue idea stage with no real inflows/outflows yet.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Current bank balances and credit lines.  
  * Expected customer payments by week (invoices, subscriptions, etc.).  
  * Recurring expenses (payroll, rent, tools) and known one-offs.  
  * A rough revenue forecast or sales plan.  
* Deliverables:  
  * 13-week forecast layout with line items grouped by inflows/outflows.  
  * Narrative summary on key risk weeks, plus 2–3 simple mitigation options.  
* SEO One-liner: “See cash problems 13 weeks before they hit with an AI-built cash flow forecast.”

---

## **FIN-02-budget-builder — Operating Budget & Scenario Template**

* Pain Point: Budgets live in one-off spreadsheets or not at all, so spending is reactive and mismatched with strategy.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without a clear budget, costs creep up and it’s hard to fund growth projects without surprises.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; big payoff in discipline and decision-making.  
* SEO Title: “AI small business budget template and scenario planner”  
* SEO Copy: “Build a simple operating budget and ‘what-if’ scenarios so you can align spend with strategy and avoid surprise overruns.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You want to plan the next year or next 12 months of spend.  
  * Costs are rising (inflation, wages, software) without clear oversight.  
  * You need a budget to share with partners, team, or lenders.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You’re still validating basic product-market fit with extremely volatile numbers.  
  * You already use formal budgeting software with mature processes.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Historic P\&L or at least 6–12 months of income and expense data.  
  * Growth plans (headcount, marketing, locations).  
  * Known constraints (covenants, cash runway, investor expectations).  
* Deliverables:  
  * Budget template with revenue, COGS, and expense categories by month/quarter.  
  * 2–3 scenario outlines (base, conservative, aggressive) with key levers annotated.  
* SEO One-liner: “Turn scattered costs into a clear, scenario-based budget you can actually run the business on.”

  * You issue invoices or run subscriptions with payment delays.  
  * Aging AR is unclear or trending up.  
  * You want to tighten DSO and improve cash conversion.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You take payment up front for everything (no AR).  
  * All revenue is collected instantly via card and there is no material AR risk.

  * Subscription or MRR data if applicable.

* Deliverables:  
  * Narrative snapshot of AR and revenue profile.  
  * Short list of suggested actions (collections focus, terms changes, etc.).

## **FIN-05-unit-economics — Unit Economics & Contribution Margin Explainer**

* Pain Point: Founders know top-line but can’t clearly explain or see per-unit profitability.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without clear unit economics, scaling can actually destroy cash and margin.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; essential for scaling decisions.  
* SEO Title: “AI unit economics and contribution margin explainer for your business”  
* SEO Copy: “Translate your revenue and cost structure into a simple unit economics view so you know if scaling each sale helps or hurts you.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re planning to scale customer acquisition.  
  * Investors or lenders ask about margins and payback.  
  * You’re debating pricing, package, or cost changes.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You truly don’t know your cost structure yet (pre-launch).  
  * Multi-product complexity makes it impossible to choose a “unit” without more work.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Revenue model (per seat, per order, per project, etc.).  
  * Direct costs per unit (COGS, service hours, variable fees).  
  * Acquisition costs, if you want to model LTV:CAC.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Simple explanation of your unit economics and contribution margin.  
  * A few sensitivity notes (e.g., what happens if cost or price shifts).  
* SEO One-liner: “Understand whether adding more customers makes or loses you money with AI-explained unit economics.”

* Pain Point: Small businesses underinvest in fraud controls until an incident happens.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Fraud, errors, and unauthorized spending can cause major financial damage and regulatory headaches.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; high protection value.  
* SEO Title: “AI small business fraud control and transaction monitoring checklist”  
* SEO Copy: “Get a practical checklist of fraud and error controls across payments, approvals, and access tailored to a small finance team.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * Multiple people make or approve payments.  
  * You’re scaling card use, reimbursements, or online payments.  
  * You’ve had anomalies or near-miss incidents.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You are highly regulated with existing detailed control frameworks.  
  * Finance processes are handled entirely by a third-party that already has controls.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Payment flows (who can pay what, how).  
  * Tools used for banking, cards, and AP/AR.  
  * Any previous fraud or error incidents.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Control checklist grouped by process (AP, AR, payroll, cash).  
  * Suggested simple monitoring practices and responsibilities.  
* SEO One-liner: “Reduce fraud and financial errors with an AI-built checklist of practical controls.”

---

## **FIN-14-tax-pack-lite — Tax Prep & Documentation Checklist**

* Pain Point: Tax time means frantic document hunts and unexpected questions from the accountant.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Missing deductions, penalties, and wasted time are common for SMBs.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; high stress reduction and potential savings.  
* SEO Title: “AI small business tax prep document checklist and info guide”  
* SEO Copy: “Prepare for tax season with a tailored document and information checklist so your accountant has what they need the first time.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You work with an accountant but always scramble at tax time.  
  * You operate multiple income streams or entities.  
  * You’ve recently added employees, locations, or new products.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You’re in a jurisdiction or structure where taxes are fully handled automatically.  
  * You are under active audit or dispute (needs direct professional counsel).  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Entity structure and jurisdiction(s).  
  * Revenue sources and approximate volume.  
  * Whether you hold inventory, assets, or employees.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Tax prep checklist grouped by category (income, expenses, payroll, assets, etc.).  
  * Simple notes on questions to clarify with your tax pro.  
* SEO One-liner: “Hit tax season prepared with an AI-generated checklist of everything your accountant will ask for.”

---

## **FIN-15-banking-stack-brief — Banking, Cards & Finance Tooling Brief**

* Pain Point: Banking, cards, and finance tools are chosen piecemeal, leading to fragmented views and extra manual work.  
* Impact Level: 7  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Fragmented finance stacks slow reporting, complicate cash management, and make funding relationships weaker.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong when you’re restructuring your stack.  
* SEO Title: “AI SMB banking and finance tech stack brief”  
* SEO Copy: “Get a tailored brief on how to structure your banking, cards, and finance tools so cash, reporting, and funding all work together.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re switching banks or adding new accounts.  
  * You’re evaluating bookkeeping, FP\&A, or spend tools.  
  * You want better integration between banking and back office.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Existing tools and relationships are working very well.  
  * You are forced into a specific provider ecosystem by regulation or contracts.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Current banks, cards, accounting, and finance tools.  
  * Key pain points (slow reporting, manual reconciliations, etc.).  
  * Growth plans and any funding relationships.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Narrative brief outlining gaps and desired capabilities.  
  * Suggested stack shape (e.g., primary bank \+ card \+ accounting \+ FP\&A \+ AR/AP layers) with selection criteria.  
* SEO One-liner: “Design a smarter banking and finance tool stack with an AI-written brief aligned to how your business runs.”

# HR \- People & HR

## **HR-01-role-scorecards — Role Scorecard & Success Profile Builder**

* Pain Point: Roles are defined as vague job titles and generic bullet lists, not clear success profiles.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Vague roles lead to mis-hires, misalignment, and poor performance conversations.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high leverage on hiring and performance.  
* SEO Title: “AI role scorecard and success profile generator for SMBs”  
* SEO Copy: “Turn fuzzy job descriptions into clear role scorecards that define responsibilities, outcomes, and what success really looks like.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re hiring for a role for the first time or revisiting a key seat.  
  * Performance issues trace back to unclear expectations.  
  * You want to align founder, manager, and candidate on what “great” means.  
* Abstain When:  
  * The role is a short-term, low-stakes gig.  
  * Your org already uses well-defined, enforced role scorecards.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Current or draft job description.  
  * Business goals the role should support.  
  * Examples of people who’ve succeeded or failed in similar roles.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Role scorecard with mission, key responsibilities, measurable outcomes, and competencies.  
  * Short “success profile” summary for job ads and onboarding.  
* SEO One-liner: “Define every role clearly with AI-built scorecards so you hire and coach to the right outcomes.”

---

## **HR-02-job-postings — Job Description & Posting Optimizer**

* Pain Point: Job postings are generic, unclear, or unattractive, leading to weak applicant pools.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Poor postings increase time-to-fill and risk bad hires; talent shortages are a top SMB issue.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong impact on inbound candidate quality.  
* SEO Title: “AI job description and job posting generator for small businesses”  
* SEO Copy: “Write clear, compelling job descriptions and postings that attract the right talent and set expectations from day one.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re opening a new role or backfilling.  
  * You get lots of unqualified applicants or very few at all.  
  * Candidates ghost or withdraw after reading the details.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Roles are filled exclusively through recruiters who control postings.  
  * You must use fixed, regulated classification language (e.g., public sector).  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Role scorecard or at least responsibilities and outcomes.  
  * Compensation range and benefits highlights.  
  * Culture and work model (remote, hybrid, on-site).  
* Deliverables:  
  * Internal job description and candidate-facing job posting copy.  
  * Optional variations for different channels (LinkedIn, niche boards, etc.).  
* SEO One-liner: “Attract better applicants with AI-written job descriptions and postings that actually resonate.”

---

## **HR-03-onboarding-checklist — Onboarding Checklist & 30/60/90 Plan**

* Pain Point: New hires show up, get a laptop and a login, and then mostly fend for themselves.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Poor onboarding is a major driver of early turnover and low engagement.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high impact on ramp time and retention.  
* SEO Title: “AI new hire onboarding checklist and 30-60-90 day plan generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Give every new hire a structured onboarding checklist and 30/60/90 day plan so they feel supported and productive faster.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re hiring more frequently.  
  * Early-stage attrition or confusion is common.  
  * You want managers to own onboarding but they lack a template.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You have a robust, standardized onboarding program that works.  
  * You’re not hiring in the foreseeable future.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Role and department.  
  * Key tools, access, and training needed.  
  * Short list of early milestones or projects.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Day 1 and week 1 onboarding checklist.  
  * Role-specific 30/60/90 day plan with goals and suggested check-ins.  
* SEO One-liner: “Reduce early attrition and ramp faster with AI-created onboarding checklists and 30/60/90 plans.”

---

## **HR-04-handbook-lite — Policies & Employee Handbook “Lite” Outline**

* Pain Point: Policies exist in scattered docs and Slack threads, not in a unified, employee-friendly reference.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Policy confusion fuels conflict, compliance risk, and inconsistent treatment.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; big upside in clarity and protection.  
* SEO Title: “AI small business employee handbook outline and policy list”  
* SEO Copy: “Draft a clear, ‘lite’ employee handbook outline so your key policies are documented, consistent, and easy to understand.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’ve grown past 5–10 people and HR questions keep popping up.  
  * You operate in multiple states or have remote employees.  
  * You’ve had near misses or worries around HR compliance.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You already have a current, lawyer-reviewed handbook.  
  * You’re in the middle of a legal dispute about existing policies (needs counsel).  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Current written policies, if any.  
  * Jurisdictions where employees work.  
  * Philosophy on time off, remote work, conduct, etc.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Handbook table of contents and section outlines.  
  * List of policy topics you need legal review on.  
* SEO One-liner: “Turn ad-hoc HR rules into a clear, AI-structured handbook outline your team can trust.”

## **HR-05-hr-ops-sops — HR Operations & People Admin SOPs**

* Pain Point: HR tasks like PTO tracking, changes, and docs are handled ad hoc, causing confusion and errors.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Botched HR ops frustrate employees, create admin drag, and increase compliance risk.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong foundation for scaling.  
* SEO Title: “AI HR operations SOP and admin checklist generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Standardize recurring HR tasks like PTO, changes, and records with clear SOPs so nothing falls through the cracks.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re big enough that HR work takes real time.  
  * PTO, records, or benefits questions constantly pop up.  
  * You’re adopting HRIS tools and want to formalize workflows.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Everything HR is still handled externally by a PEO or fully outsourced provider.  
  * You already have documented, audited HR ops procedures.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of recurring HR tasks (on/offboarding, PTO, reviews, etc.).  
  * Systems used (HRIS, payroll, benefits portals).  
  * Known process gaps or pain points.  
* Deliverables:  
  * SOPs for main HR operations workflows with step-by-step instructions and owners.  
  * Compact checklists for high-frequency tasks.  
* SEO One-liner: “Make HR admin repeatable and reliable with AI-written HR ops SOPs and checklists.”

---

## **HR-06-performance-cycles — Performance Review Cycle & Template Pack**

* Pain Point: Performance reviews are irregular, vague, or purely tied to raises.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Poor performance management fuels disengagement and uneven standards.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; key for retention and development.  
* SEO Title: “AI performance review cycle and feedback template generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Design simple but effective performance review cycles and templates that support real feedback and development—not just paperwork.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You want structured reviews (e.g., annual/biannual) but have no templates.  
  * Feedback is anecdotal and inconsistent.  
  * High performers feel unseen; low performers linger.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You already run a strong, widely accepted performance process.  
  * A global parent company mandates a non-negotiable system.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Current feedback practices and cadences.  
  * Roles and career levels (IC, manager, etc.).  
  * Values or competencies you want evaluated.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Review cycle outline (timing, participants, steps).  
  * Self-review, manager review, and peer feedback templates.  
* SEO One-liner: “Upgrade performance reviews from awkward rituals to useful conversations with AI-crafted cycles and templates.”

---

## **HR-07-engagement-pulses — Engagement Pulse Survey & Insight Summary**

* Pain Point: Leadership senses burnout or disengagement but lacks structured feedback.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Burnout and low engagement drive turnover, productivity loss, and culture drift.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high when tied to action.  
* SEO Title: “AI employee engagement pulse survey and insight generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Create short, targeted pulse surveys and turn responses into a clear engagement insight summary with suggested actions.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You see signs of burnout or morale issues.  
  * You’re scaling headcount, changing strategy, or shifting work models.  
  * Retention is becoming a concern.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You’re in crisis or layoffs where surveys could cause more fear.  
  * You have no intention or capacity to act on feedback yet.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Size and structure of your team.  
  * Known stress points (pay, workload, leadership, etc.).  
  * Frequency you’d realistically run pulses (monthly, quarterly).  
* Deliverables:  
  * 10–20 question pulse survey tailored to your context.  
  * Insight summary format with categories (what’s working, what’s not, actions).  
* SEO One-liner: “Detect burnout and engagement issues early with AI-designed pulse surveys and insight summaries.”

---

## **HR-08-people-analytics-lite — People Analytics “Lite” Snapshot**

* Pain Point: People decisions rely purely on gut instead of basic data patterns.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without data, issues like pay inequity, turnover risk, and skill gaps stay hidden.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong for prioritizing HR focus.  
* SEO Title: “AI lite people analytics snapshot for small teams”  
* SEO Copy: “Turn simple HR data—headcount, attrition, tenure, performance—into a people analytics snapshot with clear priorities.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You have at least 10–15 people and some history.  
  * Turnover, absenteeism, or performance variance is noticeable.  
  * You want to make more evidence-based HR decisions.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Team is tiny or brand new with almost no history.  
  * Data is scattered or unreliable (fix data first).  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Basic employee list with start dates, roles, compensation, and status.  
  * Any performance or engagement data you have.  
  * Headcount changes over the last 12–24 months.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Narrative snapshot highlighting patterns (attrition, tenure, concentration, etc.).  
  * A handful of recommended HR focus areas (e.g., leveling, manager support, pay bands).  
* SEO One-liner: “See your workforce patterns clearly with an AI-written people analytics snapshot.”

---

## **HR-09-learning-paths — Role-Based Learning Path & Skill Map**

* Pain Point: Employees want growth, but there’s no clear path for skills or advancement.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Lack of development drives attrition and skills gaps, especially around digital and AI skills.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; major impact on retention and upskilling.  
* SEO Title: “AI role-based learning path and skill development planner”  
* SEO Copy: “Map out simple learning paths and skill milestones for each role so employees see a future and know how to grow.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * Key employees ask “what’s next for me?”  
  * You struggle to fill roles internally due to skill gaps.  
  * You want to support AI/digital upskilling.  
* Abstain When:  
  * Company growth is frozen and advancement is unlikely short-term.  
  * Roles are extremely bespoke with no repeatable patterns.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Role definitions and core responsibilities.  
  * Skills required for each role and level.  
  * Budget and platforms for learning (courses, internal mentoring, etc.).  
* Deliverables:  
  * Role-based learning path with stages, skills, and suggested learning activities.  
  * Simple progression outline (e.g., junior → mid → senior) where applicable.  
* SEO One-liner: “Give employees a clear growth path with AI-designed learning and skill maps per role.”

## **HR-10-hr-okrs — HR & People OKR Starter Pack**

* Pain Point: HR work is viewed as “soft” and invisible instead of tied to measurable business outcomes.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without clear HR objectives, people initiatives stay reactive and under-resourced.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; high when leadership buys in.  
* SEO Title: “AI HR OKR and people strategy objective generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Draft focused HR and people OKRs that connect hiring, engagement, and development to business goals.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You use OKRs or goal-setting elsewhere in the business.  
  * You want HR/People to have a clear, strategic plan.  
  * You’re tackling big challenges (scaling headcount, burnout, culture changes).  
* Abstain When:  
  * You don’t use any formal goal framework.  
  * Strategy is in flux and priorities change monthly.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Company-level goals for the next 6–12 months.  
  * Current HR pain points (hiring, retention, engagement, etc.).  
  * Rough capacity of people handling HR.  
* Deliverables:  
  * 3–7 HR/People OKRs with measurable key results.  
  * Short list of initiatives linked to each OKR.  
* SEO One-liner: “Make HR a true growth engine with AI-written OKRs tied directly to your business goals.”

# PDT \- Product & Strategy

## **PDT-01-roadmap-compiler — Product Roadmap Compiler & Narrative**

* Pain Point: Ideas live in scattered docs and heads, not in a coherent roadmap everyone can see and act on.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without a clear roadmap, teams thrash between priorities, ship the wrong things, and slow time-to-value.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; huge payoff in focus and alignment.  
* SEO Title: “AI product roadmap generator and narrative explainer”  
* SEO Copy: “Turn scattered product ideas and projects into a structured roadmap with a clear narrative that aligns founders, teams, and stakeholders.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You have a backlog of ideas but no coherent plan.  
  * Stakeholders ask, “What’s coming when?” and you hesitate.  
  * You’re planning the next 2–4 quarters of product work.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You’re pre-product or still validating basic problem/solution.  
  * You already maintain a robust, widely trusted roadmap.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of current and proposed initiatives/features.  
  * Business goals and themes for the next 6–12 months.  
  * Rough capacity constraints (team size, sprints, key dates).  
* Deliverables:  
  * Narrative roadmap (by theme, quarter, or milestone) describing what and why.  
  * Structural outline you can drop into your roadmap tool (e.g., lanes, columns).  
* SEO One-liner: “Compile all your product ideas into a clear AI-written roadmap and story everyone can follow.”

---

## **PDT-02-prioritization-matrix — Roadmap Prioritization Matrix & Scoring**

* Pain Point: Everything feels “priority one,” so nothing truly gets prioritized.  
* Impact Level: 10  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Poor prioritization wastes dev cycles and delays high-ROI features.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high leverage on impact per sprint.  
* SEO Title: “AI product prioritization matrix and scoring model for SMBs”  
* SEO Copy: “Score and rank your product ideas using simple frameworks so you build the highest-impact features first with fewer debates.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You have more ideas than capacity.  
  * Stakeholders disagree about what to build next.  
  * You want to move from “gut feel” to transparent criteria.  
* Abstain When:  
  * You have only a handful of must-do items and limited complexity.  
  * Your roadmap is fully dictated by external contracts/regulators.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Backlog list (features, projects, experiments).  
  * Strategic goals (e.g., activation, retention, ARPU, new segments).  
  * Constraints and relevant impact dimensions (customer value, revenue, risk, effort, etc.).  
* Deliverables:  
  * Prioritization model description (e.g., RICE/weighted scoring) and criteria definitions.  
  * Ranked list of items with scores to plug into a spreadsheet or PM tool.  
* SEO One-liner: “Stop arguing about what to build next with an AI-built prioritization matrix and scored backlog.”

---

## **PDT-03-feedback-synthesizer — Product Feedback Synthesizer & Theme Map**

* Pain Point: Customer feedback piles up in tickets, calls, and reviews but rarely gets systematically synthesized.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Ignored feedback leads to churn, missed opportunities, and building features no one asked for.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; very high insight density.  
* SEO Title: “AI product feedback analysis and feature theme generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Turn messy customer feedback into clear themes, pain points, and feature ideas so product decisions are grounded in real user signals.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You have NPS comments, support tickets, call notes, or reviews.  
  * Product decisions feel detached from actual customer voice.  
  * You’re planning a roadmap refresh or new version.  
* Abstain When:  
  * User base is too tiny or feedback volume is near-zero.  
  * Feedback is extremely sensitive/confidential and cannot be shared with tools.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Text exports of feedback sources (surveys, tickets, calls, reviews).  
  * Basic customer segmentation (plan, industry, role, etc.), if available.  
  * Current product areas/modules and known “hot” topics.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Theme map summarizing key issues, requests, and delights.  
  * Short list of top candidate initiatives tied to feedback themes.  
* SEO One-liner: “Convert raw feedback into an AI-written map of product themes and high-value feature ideas.”

---

## **PDT-04-vision-brief — Product Vision & Positioning Brief**

* Pain Point: The product vision lives mostly in the founder’s head and is hard to communicate consistently.  
* Impact Level: 9  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without a crisp vision and positioning, teams ship incoherent features and messaging stays generic.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium–high; foundational for long-term product and GTM.  
* SEO Title: “AI product vision and positioning brief generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Turn your scattered ideas into a clear product vision and positioning brief that guides what you build and how you talk about it.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re repositioning, entering a new market, or refining who you serve.  
  * Marketing, sales, and product describe the product differently.  
  * You’re hiring and need to tell the story consistently.  
* Abstain When:  
  * The product is still extremely experimental and pivots weekly.  
  * You’re forced to follow corporate parent positioning verbatim.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * Current positioning statements, if any, and product description.  
  * ICP/segments and key problems you solve.  
  * Competitive context and unique strengths.  
* Deliverables:  
  * Product vision statement, positioning summary, and key messaging pillars.  
  * Short “elevator narratives” tailored to customers, investors, and team.  
* SEO One-liner: “Align your team around a sharp product vision and positioning brief generated by AI.”

---

## **PDT-05-bets-portfolio — Strategic Bets & Portfolio Map**

* Pain Point: Strategy discussions oscillate between tiny tasks and huge dreams without a clear view of “bets” across horizons.  
* Impact Level: 8  
* Time/Revenue Impact: Without a portfolio view, businesses either over-focus on today (no innovation) or chase too many speculative bets.  
* Effort vs. Value: Medium; strong for strategic clarity and risk balance.  
* SEO Title: “AI strategic bets portfolio and roadmap lanes generator”  
* SEO Copy: “Map your near-term, mid-term, and long-term product bets into a simple portfolio view so you balance stability with innovation.”  
* Deploy When:  
  * You’re juggling core improvements, new features, and experimental ideas.  
  * Leadership wants a clearer strategy narrative for the next 1–3 years.  
  * You’re considering big moves (new product line, vertical, or geography).  
* Abstain When:  
  * You’re very early and still trying to get one thing working.  
  * All work is dictated by a single massive contract with no real choice.  
* Pre-Flight Inventory:  
  * List of current and future initiatives (including “moonshots”).  
  * Time horizons you care about (e.g., now, next, later).  
  * Strategic themes (e.g., retention, expansion, new markets, ops efficiency).  
* Deliverables:  
  * Strategic bets portfolio map grouped by horizon and risk/impact.  
  * Short narrative connecting bets back to business goals and constraints.
